# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--50ea83e6` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--50ea83e6$` filter
- `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--7b8baff1` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--7b8baff1$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--50ea83e6`, `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--7b8baff1`

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress.      1→# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide
     2→## Upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0
     3→
     4→## Overview
     5→
     6→This migration guide covers the upgrade of the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The 1.31.0 release introduces enhanced route cache management with a new enum-based approach, support for observability mode with deferred stream closure, and improved stream lifecycle management.
     7→
     8→Key highlights of this release:
     9→- **New `route_cache_action` enum** replaces boolean flag-based route cache control
    10→- **Observability mode enhancements** with deferred stream closure and configurable timeouts
    11→- **Improved stream management** via thread-local stream managers for better resource cleanup
    12→
    13→Most configurations will continue to work with minimal or no changes, though some optimizations are recommended for new deployments.
    14→
    15→---
    16→
    17→## Breaking Changes
    18→
    19→### 1. Route Cache Control Field Reorganization
    20→
    21→**What changed:**
    22→- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11 in v1.30) is being **transitioned to a new enum-based system** using `route_cache_action` (field 18 in v1.31)
    23→- A new `RouteCacheAction` enum provides three explicit states instead of just binary on/off
    24→
    25→**Migration impact:** ⚠️ **Low to Moderate**
    26→- Existing configurations using `disable_clear_route_cache` will **continue to work** due to backward compatibility
    27→- However, Envoy's internal code now treats these as different representations that may not remain synchronized in future versions
    28→- New configurations should use the enum approach
    29→
 
... (truncated)
54-assistanttool_useBash
55-usertool_resultBash
760 /workspace/documentation.md
A: Ask: "Does my external processor ever modify headers that affect routing decisions?" If yes and selectively, use `DEFAULT`. If always, use `CLEAR`. If never, use `RETAIN`.

**Q: Can I change `route_cache_action` at runtime?**
A: Not directly via admin API in v1.31. You must update the configuration and perform a graceful reload (`SIGHUP` on process ID or configuration push through control plane).

**Q: What's the performance impact of changing from `RETAIN` to `CLEAR`?**
A: Minimal direct impact from the enum choice itself. The performance difference comes from increased route recomputation frequency. Measure route cache hit ratio before/after.

---

## Summary Checklist

Use this checklist for your migration:

- [ ] **Audit:** Found and documented all `disable_clear_route_cache` usage
- [ ] **Plan:** Decided on appropriate `route_cache_action` for each config
- [ ] **Update:** Migrated configurations to v1.31 style or verified backward compatibility
- [ ] **Validate:** Ran configuration validator and resolved any conflicts
- [ ] **Test:** Tested in staging with representative traffic
- [ ] **Monitor:** Set up dashboards for route cache and ext_proc statistics
- [ ] **Deploy:** Canary deployment to one instance
- [ ] **Observe:** Monitored metrics for 10-15 minutes
- [ ] **Rollout:** Gradual rollout to remaining instances
- [ ] **Document:** Updated internal documentation with new configuration approach
- [ ] **Archive:** Backed up v1.30 configurations for rollback if needed

---

**Last Updated:** 2024
**Envoy Versions:** v1.30.0 → v1.31.0

[#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. If not set, all headers may be modified except\\n156:   // for \\\"host\\\", \\\":authority\\\", \\\":scheme\\\", \\\":method\\\", and headers that start\\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\\n159:   // (which is usually \\\"x-envoy\\\").\\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \\\"host\\\" or \\\":authority\\\" may not in itself\\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. There will be no\\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\\n202: \\n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\\n205: \\n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \\\"Send and Go\\\" mode that can be used\\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\\n209:   //\\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\\n212:   //\\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\\n214:   // This also means that\\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\\n217:   //\\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n219:   //\\n220:   // .. warning::\\n221:   //\\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n227:   //\\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n229: }\\n230: \\n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n232: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\\n233: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\\n234: message MetadataOptions {\\n235:   message MetadataNamespaces {\\n236:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n237:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\\n238:     repeated string untyped = 1;\\n239: \\n240:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n241:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n259: //\\n260: // This works as below:\\n261: //\\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n265: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\\n266: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n267: //   4. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n118: \n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n122: \n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n129: \n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n136: \n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n147:     gte {}\n148:   }];\n149: \n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\n153: \n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n156:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n159:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n166: \n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n172:     gte {}\n173:   }];\n174: \n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n179: \n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n183: \n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n188: \n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n195: \n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n202: \n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n205: \n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n209:   //\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n212:   //\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n214:   // This also means that\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n217:   //\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n219:   //\n220:   // .. warning::\n221:   //\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n227:   //\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\n229: }\n230: \n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n232: // dynamic metadata. envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n141:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n142: \n143:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n144:   // for expressive policies. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n270: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\n271: message MetadataOptions {\n272:   message MetadataNamespaces {\n273:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n274:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n275:     repeated string untyped = 1;\n276: \n277:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n278:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n279:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n280:     // definition for safe parsing.\n281:     repeated string typed = 2;\n282:   }\n283: \n284:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n285:   // the external processing server.\n286:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n287: \n288:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n289:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n292: }\n293: \n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n296: //\n297: // This works as below:\n298: //\n299: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n300: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n301: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n302: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n303: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n304: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n305: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n306: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n307:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n308:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n309:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n310: \n311:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n312:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n313:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n314: }\n315: \n316: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n317: // virtual host or cluster.\n318: message ExtProcPerRoute {\n319:   oneof override {\n320:     option (validate.required) = true;\n321: \n322:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n323:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n324:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n325: \n326:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n327:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n328:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\n329:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n330:   }\n331: }\n332: \n333: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n334: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n335: message ExtProcOverrides {\n336:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n337:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n338: \n339:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n340:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n341:   bool async_mode = 2;\n342: \n343:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n344:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n345:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\n346:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n347: \n348:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n349:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n350:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\n351:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n352: \n353:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n354:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n355: \n356:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n357:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n358:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n359:   // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n360:   // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n361:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n362: \n363:   // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n364:   // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\n365:   // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\n366:   // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\n367:   repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\n368: }\n369: ",

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\\n55: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--7b8baff1@7d6a8ad71741583b3a75f94937b6f294b39e2667/-/blob/docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst\"}",
  "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ",

  "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## Upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the upgrade of the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The 1.31.0 release introduces enhanced route cache management with a new enum-based approach, support for observability mode with deferred stream closure, and improved stream lifecycle management.\n\nKey highlights of this release:\n- **New `route_cache_action` enum** replaces boolean flag-based route cache control\n- **Observability mode enhancements** with deferred stream closure and configurable timeouts\n- **Improved stream management** via thread-local stream managers for better resource cleanup\n\nMost configurations will continue to work with minimal or no changes, though some optimizations are recommended for new deployments.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Control Field Reorganization\n\n**What changed:**\n- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11 in v1.30) is being **transitioned to a new enum-based system** using `route_cache_action` (field 18 in v1.31)\n- A new `RouteCacheAction` enum provides three explicit states instead of just binary on/off\n\n**Migration impact:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Low to Moderate**\n- Existing configurations using `disable_clear_route_cache` will **continue to work** due to backward compatibility\n- However, Envoy's internal code now treats these as different representations that may not remain synchronized in future versions\n- New configurations should use the enum approach\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31 - Recommended):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Mapping reference:**\n| v1.30 Config | v1.31 Equivalent | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear route cache |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Clear route cache per ext_proc response |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Always clear route cache *(new in v1.31)* |\n\n**RouteCacheAction Enum Definition:**\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: Clear route cache only when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache flag\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  // Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n**Important: Mutual Exclusivity**\n- Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` can be set in a configuration\n- If both are present, the configuration will be rejected at validation time\n- The new `route_cache_action` field is marked with migration annotation `[(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"]`\n\n---\n\n### 2. Filter Method Signature Changes (for filter extensions)\n\n**What changed:**\n- The `sendTrailers()` method signature was updated to support observability mode\n- Stream pointer type changed from `std::unique_ptr` to raw pointer in internal implementation\n\n**Migration impact:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Only affects custom filter extensions**\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```cpp\nvoid sendTrailers(ProcessorState& state, const Http::HeaderMap& trailers);\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```cpp\nvoid sendTrailers(ProcessorState& state, const Http::HeaderMap& trailers,\n                  bool observability_mode = false);\n```\n\n**Note:** This change only affects organizations that have custom extensions or derivations of the ext_proc filter. Standard Envoy deployments using the filter through configuration are unaffected.\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### disable_clear_route_cache (Soft Deprecation)\n\n**Status:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Soft deprecation** - Still functional, but superseded by newer field\n\n**Details:**\n- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is not formally deprecated, but is now handled through the `route_cache_action` enum\n- The field remains for backward compatibility\n- Envoy logs and internal handling now recommend using `route_cache_action` in documentation\n\n**Migration path:**\n```yaml\n# Old approach (v1.30 compatible, but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# New approach (v1.31, recommended for new configs)\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n\n# New explicit approach (v1.31, recommended for complex scenarios)\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear cache\n```\n\n**Timeline:**\n- v1.31.0: Both fields supported, `route_cache_action` recommended\n- v1.32.0+: Expected to remain backward compatible, but watch release notes\n- Future major version: May be removed entirely\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Enhanced Route Cache Action Control\n\n**What's new:**\n- Explicit `route_cache_action` enum replacing implicit boolean logic\n- Three distinct states for fine-grained control over route cache lifecycle\n\n**Use cases:**\n\n**Scenario A: Default Behavior (Responsive)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache clears only when external processor explicitly requests it\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\nUse when: External processor makes intelligent decisions about when route recomputation is needed\n\n**Scenario B: Always Clear (Aggressive)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache always clears, forcing immediate route recomputation\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\nUse when: External processor may modify headers that affect routing, and you want maximum responsiveness\nExample: Auth-based routing where authorization headers are modified\n\n**Scenario C: Never Clear (Conservative)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache never clears, maximizing performance\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\nUse when: External processor never modifies routing-affecting headers, or you want to prioritize cache efficiency\nExample: Logging/monitoring-only external processor\n\n---\n\n### 2. Observability Mode with Deferred Stream Closure\n\n**What's new:**\n- `observability_mode: true` enables \"send and go\" behavior\n- External processor streams can be kept open longer than the main request/response flow\n- New `deferred_close_timeout` field controls how long streams are held open before closure\n\n**How it works:**\n\nIn observability mode:\n1. Envoy sends request and response data to the external processor without waiting for responses\n2. The external processor acts as a passive observer/logger\n3. The gRPC stream remains open after the request/response completes (deferred closure)\n4. Stream closes after `deferred_close_timeout` expires (default: 5 seconds)\n\n**Configuration:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Optional, default is 5000ms\n\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Processing mode restrictions in observability mode:**\n- \u2705 Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is fully supported\n- \u2705 `NONE` mode (skip body) works as expected\n- \u26a0\ufe0f Other modes (`BUFFERED`, `BUFFERED_PARTIAL`) are ignored; behavior falls back to streaming\n\n**Key behavioral differences:**\n- External processor should **not** send responses (they are ignored)\n- `message_timeout` restrictions don't apply (stream remains open indefinitely until deferred timeout)\n- Flow control is still being developed; use with caution on high-throughput systems (see GitHub issue #33319)\n\n**New configuration fields:**\n\n| Field | Type | Default | Description |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `observability_mode` | bool | false | Enable send-and-go observation mode |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | Duration | 5000ms | How long to keep stream open after request/response completes |\n\n**Example use cases:**\n- Passive telemetry collection\n- Non-invasive traffic monitoring\n- Distributed tracing integration\n- Observability data extraction without modifying traffic\n\n---\n\n### 3. Thread-Local Stream Management\n\n**What's new:**\n- Internal stream management improvements for observability mode\n- `ThreadLocalStreamManager` handles deferred stream cleanup\n- Improved resource management for long-lived streams\n\n**Impact on configuration:**\n- This is an internal implementation detail\n- No configuration changes needed\n- Automatically used when `observability_mode` is enabled\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Audit Current Route Cache Configuration\n\n1. Review all ext_proc filter configurations in your environment:\n   ```bash\n   # Search for ext_proc filters in your configs\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" *.yaml\n   ```\n\n2. Note which configurations use `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### Step 2: Plan Route Cache Strategy\n\nFor each configuration with `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:\n\n| Current Behavior | New Configuration | Rationale |\n|---|---|---|\n| External processor never modifies routing headers | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Preserve performance optimization |\n| External processor sometimes modifies routing headers | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Let processor control cache |\n| External processor always affects routing | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Ensure correct routing decisions |\n\n### Step 3: Update Configuration Files\n\n**Example migration:**\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n### Step 4: Optional - Enable Observability Mode (for new deployments)\n\nIf you need non-invasive monitoring:\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      observability_mode: true\n      deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: STREAMED\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### Step 5: Validate Configuration\n\n1. Validate YAML syntax:\n   ```bash\n   envoy -c config.yaml --mode validate_config\n   ```\n\n2. Check for configuration conflicts:\n   - Ensure only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` is set\n   - If observability mode is enabled, verify processing mode is compatible\n\n3. Test in staging environment with representative traffic\n\n### Step 6: Deploy and Monitor\n\n1. Deploy updated configuration to one canary instance\n2. Monitor for:\n   - Route cache hit/miss ratios\n   - Ext_proc filter statistics (clear_route_cache_* counters)\n   - gRPC stream health\n3. Gradually roll out to remaining instances\n4. Compare performance metrics before/after\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Configuration Validation Tests\n\n**Test mutual exclusivity:**\n```bash\n# This should fail validation\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Test enum values:**\n```bash\n# Test each value separately\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 2. Route Cache Behavior Tests\n\n**Scenario: DEFAULT behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\nExpected: Route cache clears when external processor response has `clear_route_cache: true`\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache should clear\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache should remain\n- \u2705 Returns with no cache directive \u2192 cache should remain\n\n**Scenario: CLEAR behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\nExpected: Route cache always clears regardless of processor response\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache clears (expected)\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache still clears (verify this works)\n\n**Scenario: RETAIN behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\nExpected: Route cache never clears\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache should NOT clear\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache should NOT clear\n\n### 3. Observability Mode Tests\n\n**Test configuration validation:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 3s\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: STREAMED  # \u2705 OK\n  response_body_mode: BUFFERED # \u26a0\ufe0f Will be ignored\n```\n\n**Test stream lifecycle:**\n1. Start Envoy with observability_mode enabled\n2. Send request through proxy\n3. Monitor gRPC stream:\n   - Stream should remain open after response completes\n   - Stream should close after `deferred_close_timeout` expires\n4. Verify external processor receives all data without responding\n\n**Test flow control (with caution):**\n- Send high-volume traffic through observability mode\n- Monitor for buffer overflow or dropped messages\n- Check warning at GitHub issue #33319\n\n### 4. Backward Compatibility Tests\n\n**Test old configuration still works:**\n```yaml\n# v1.30 style should still work\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\nExpected: Configuration loads without error and behaves like `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n### 5. Performance Tests\n\n**Before/after comparison:**\n\n| Metric | Target | How to measure |\n|---|---|---|\n| Route cache hit ratio | \u2265 95% (RETAIN) | Envoy admin /stats with cache stats |\n| Ext_proc latency | < 200ms p99 | external_processor.message_timeout_ms metric |\n| gRPC stream count | Stable | Prometheus or Envoy /stats |\n| Memory usage | \u00b1 5% | Container memory usage |\n\n**Test scenarios:**\n1. Conservative (RETAIN) vs. default behavior \u2192 expect better cache hit ratio\n2. Aggressive (CLEAR) vs. default \u2192 expect more route recomputations\n3. Observability mode without request/response body \u2192 expect lower latency than normal mode\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Quick Rollback (Less than 1 minute downtime)\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrade:\n\n1. **Immediately revert configuration:**\n   ```yaml\n   # Instead of new style:\n   # route_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n   # Use old compatible style:\n   disable_clear_route_cache: false\n   ```\n\n2. **Reload Envoy without restart:**\n   ```bash\n   kill -HUP <envoy_pid>  # Graceful reload\n   ```\n\n3. **Verify service health:**\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep ext_proc\n   ```\n\n### Extended Rollback (Staged revert)\n\nIf using infrastructure as code:\n\n1. Revert configuration files to v1.30 versions\n2. Perform canary deployment on one instance\n3. Monitor for stability (5-10 minutes)\n4. Complete rollback to remaining instances\n\n### Full Version Rollback (if needed)\n\nIf issues are critical:\n\n1. Preserve data/state from v1.31 deployment\n2. Download v1.30.0 binary (if still available)\n3. Deploy v1.30.0 with previous configuration\n4. Investigate root cause before re-upgrading\n\n**Recovery steps post-rollback:**\n- Check Envoy logs for configuration errors\n- Verify external processor service compatibility\n- Review any custom filter extensions for compatibility\n- Test thoroughly in staging before retry\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Using Both Fields Simultaneously\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflict!\n```\n\n**Solution:**\nChoose one approach. The configuration validator will catch this:\n```yaml\n# Choose EITHER the old style:\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# OR the new style:\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Wrong RouteCacheAction for Use Case\n\n**Problem:**\nUsing `CLEAR` when external processor only logs traffic, causing unnecessary route recomputation overhead.\n\n**Solution:**\nProfile your external processor behavior:\n```bash\n# In your processor, log which responses set clear_route_cache\nlog.info(\"Request headers changed: {}\", header_modified)\n```\n\nThen use appropriate action:\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN  # If processor doesn't modify routing headers\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT # If processor selectively modifies headers\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR   # If processor often modifies routing headers\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Observability Mode Without Proper Timeouts\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\n# deferred_close_timeout not set (uses default 5s)\n```\nMay cause unexpected stream behavior if not aligned with request timeouts.\n\n**Solution:**\nExplicitly set timeout matching your infrastructure:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Explicit for observability\n```\n\nEnsure it's longer than typical response time but shorter than upstream timeouts.\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode with Incompatible Body Modes\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: BUFFERED  # Not officially supported in observability mode\n```\n\n**Solution:**\nUse only STREAMED mode:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: STREAMED   # \u2705 Correct\n  response_body_mode: STREAMED  # \u2705 Correct\n```\n\n---\n\n## Statistics Changes\n\n### New Statistics in v1.31\n\nThe ext_proc filter continues to use the same statistics namespace but handles route cache events differently based on the new `route_cache_action` enum.\n\n**Existing statistics still available:**\n- `clear_route_cache_ignored` - Requests to clear cache that were ignored\n- `clear_route_cache_disabled` - Cache clears that were explicitly disabled\n\n**Behavioral change:**\nWhen using `route_cache_action`:\n- If set to `RETAIN`, all external processor requests to clear cache are counted in `clear_route_cache_disabled`\n- If set to `CLEAR`, cache is always cleared (fewer `clear_route_cache_ignored` events)\n- If set to `DEFAULT`, behavior matches v1.30\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Reference\n\n### Complete v1.31 ext_proc Configuration Example\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n\n      # Required: gRPC service configuration\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n        timeout: 2s\n\n      # Optional: how to handle processor unavailability\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n\n      # Optional: route cache control (choose ONE)\n      # New style (recommended):\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN  # DEFAULT, CLEAR, or RETAIN\n\n      # Old style (still supported, but deprecated):\n      # disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n      # Optional: processing mode configuration\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        response_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        request_trailer_mode: SEND\n        response_trailer_mode: SKIP\n\n      # Optional: attributes to send to processor\n      request_attributes:\n        - request.path\n        - request.method\n      response_attributes:\n        - response.code\n\n      # Optional: mutation rules for headers\n      mutation_rules:\n        allow_all_routing: false\n        allow_envoy: true\n        allow_other_origins: false\n\n      # Optional: header forwarding rules\n      forward_rules:\n        allowed_headers:\n          patterns:\n            - prefix: \"x-custom\"\n\n      # Optional: observability mode\n      observability_mode: false\n      deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n\n      # Optional: metadata handling\n      metadata_options:\n        forwarding_namespaces:\n          untyped:\n            - \"my.custom.namespace\"\n        receiving_namespaces:\n          untyped:\n            - \"ext_proc_result\"\n\n      # Optional: statistics prefix (to distinguish multiple ext_proc filters)\n      stat_prefix: \"my_ext_proc_\"\n\n      # Optional: additional filter state metadata\n      filter_metadata:\n        version: \"1.31\"\n        environment: \"production\"\n\n      # Optional: allow external processor to override processing mode\n      allow_mode_override: true\n\n      # Optional: ignore immediate_response from processor\n      disable_immediate_response: false\n\n      # Optional: max override timeout allowed from processor\n      max_message_timeout: 30s\n\n      # Message timeout for each gRPC message\n      message_timeout: 200ms\n```\n\n---\n\n## Version Compatibility Matrix\n\n| Component | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Proto API version | v3 | v3 | Same major version |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2705 Full support | \u2705 Supported (legacy) | Transitional in v1.31 |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 Full support | New in v1.31 |\n| `observability_mode` | \u2705 Present | \u2705 Enhanced | Stream lifecycle improved |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 New | Controls observability mode timing |\n| External processor protocol | gRPC v1 | gRPC v1 | No protocol changes |\n| Backward config compat | N/A | \u2705 High | Old configs work mostly as-is |\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n### Proto Definitions\n- **Configuration:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- **Processing Mode:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto`\n\n### Implementation Files\n- **Filter Header:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n- **Filter Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n- **Configuration:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/config.cc`\n\n### Documentation\n- **Filter Documentation:** `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`\n- **API Reference:** Envoy v3 API reference for ExternalProcessor message\n\n### Related Issues\n- **GitHub #33319:** Flow control in observability mode (still in development)\n- **Proto Migration Annotations:** `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto`\n\n---\n\n## FAQ\n\n**Q: Can I use both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` in the same config?**\nA: No. The configuration validator will reject configurations that set both fields. Choose one approach based on your version and compatibility needs.\n\n**Q: Is observability mode production-ready in v1.31.0?**\nA: Yes, but with a caveat. The feature is production-ready for basic use (reading logs/metrics). However, flow control mechanisms are still being developed (GitHub issue #33319), so use caution with extremely high-throughput systems.\n\n**Q: What happens if I set an invalid `route_cache_action` value?**\nA: Configuration validation will fail during startup with a clear error message. Valid values are `DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, or `RETAIN`.\n\n**Q: Do I need to change my external processor code?**\nA: No. The external processor protocol (gRPC messages) hasn't changed between v1.30 and v1.31. Your processor code should work without modification.\n\n**Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?**\nA: Ask: \"Does my external processor ever modify headers that affect routing decisions?\" If yes and selectively, use `DEFAULT`. If always, use `CLEAR`. If never, use `RETAIN`.\n\n**Q: Can I change `route_cache_action` at runtime?**\nA: Not directly via admin API in v1.31. You must update the configuration and perform a graceful reload (`SIGHUP` on process ID or configuration push through control plane).\n\n**Q: What's the performance impact of changing from `RETAIN` to `CLEAR`?**\nA: Minimal direct impact from the enum choice itself. The performance difference comes from increased route recomputation frequency. Measure route cache hit ratio before/after.\n\n---\n\n## Summary Checklist\n\nUse this checklist for your migration:\n\n- [ ] **Audit:** Found and documented all `disable_clear_route_cache` usage\n- [ ] **Plan:** Decided on appropriate `route_cache_action` for each config\n- [ ] **Update:** Migrated configurations to v1.31 style or verified backward compatibility\n- [ ] **Validate:** Ran configuration validator and resolved any conflicts\n- [ ] **Test:** Tested in staging with representative traffic\n- [ ] **Monitor:** Set up dashboards for route cache and ext_proc statistics\n- [ ] **Deploy:** Canary deployment to one instance\n- [ ] **Observe:** Monitored metrics for 10-15 minutes\n- [ ] **Rollout:** Gradual rollout to remaining instances\n- [ ] **Document:** Updated internal documentation with new configuration approach\n- [ ] **Archive:** Backed up v1.30 configurations for rollback if needed\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated:** 2024\n**Envoy Versions:** v1.30.0 \u2192 v1.31.0\n",
