{
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## Upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the upgrade of the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The 1.31.0 release introduces enhanced route cache management with a new enum-based approach, support for observability mode with deferred stream closure, and improved stream lifecycle management.\n\nKey highlights of this release:\n- **New `route_cache_action` enum** replaces boolean flag-based route cache control\n- **Observability mode enhancements** with deferred stream closure and configurable timeouts\n- **Improved stream management** via thread-local stream managers for better resource cleanup\n\nMost configurations will continue to work with minimal or no changes, though some optimizations are recommended for new deployments.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Control Field Reorganization\n\n**What changed:**\n- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11 in v1.30) is being **transitioned to a new enum-based system** using `route_cache_action` (field 18 in v1.31)\n- A new `RouteCacheAction` enum provides three explicit states instead of just binary on/off\n\n**Migration impact:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Low to Moderate**\n- Existing configurations using `disable_clear_route_cache` will **continue to work** due to backward compatibility\n- However, Envoy's internal code now treats these as different representations that may not remain synchronized in future versions\n- New configurations should use the enum approach\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31 - Recommended):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Mapping reference:**\n| v1.30 Config | v1.31 Equivalent | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear route cache |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Clear route cache per ext_proc response |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Always clear route cache *(new in v1.31)* |\n\n**RouteCacheAction Enum Definition:**\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: Clear route cache only when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache flag\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  // Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n**Important: Mutual Exclusivity**\n- Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` can be set in a configuration\n- If both are present, the configuration will be rejected at validation time\n- The new `route_cache_action` field is marked with migration annotation `[(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"]`\n\n---\n\n### 2. Filter Method Signature Changes (for filter extensions)\n\n**What changed:**\n- The `sendTrailers()` method signature was updated to support observability mode\n- Stream pointer type changed from `std::unique_ptr` to raw pointer in internal implementation\n\n**Migration impact:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Only affects custom filter extensions**\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```cpp\nvoid sendTrailers(ProcessorState& state, const Http::HeaderMap& trailers);\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```cpp\nvoid sendTrailers(ProcessorState& state, const Http::HeaderMap& trailers,\n                  bool observability_mode = false);\n```\n\n**Note:** This change only affects organizations that have custom extensions or derivations of the ext_proc filter. Standard Envoy deployments using the filter through configuration are unaffected.\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### disable_clear_route_cache (Soft Deprecation)\n\n**Status:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Soft deprecation** - Still functional, but superseded by newer field\n\n**Details:**\n- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is not formally deprecated, but is now handled through the `route_cache_action` enum\n- The field remains for backward compatibility\n- Envoy logs and internal handling now recommend using `route_cache_action` in documentation\n\n**Migration path:**\n```yaml\n# Old approach (v1.30 compatible, but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# New approach (v1.31, recommended for new configs)\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n\n# New explicit approach (v1.31, recommended for complex scenarios)\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear cache\n```\n\n**Timeline:**\n- v1.31.0: Both fields supported, `route_cache_action` recommended\n- v1.32.0+: Expected to remain backward compatible, but watch release notes\n- Future major version: May be removed entirely\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Enhanced Route Cache Action Control\n\n**What's new:**\n- Explicit `route_cache_action` enum replacing implicit boolean logic\n- Three distinct states for fine-grained control over route cache lifecycle\n\n**Use cases:**\n\n**Scenario A: Default Behavior (Responsive)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache clears only when external processor explicitly requests it\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\nUse when: External processor makes intelligent decisions about when route recomputation is needed\n\n**Scenario B: Always Clear (Aggressive)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache always clears, forcing immediate route recomputation\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\nUse when: External processor may modify headers that affect routing, and you want maximum responsiveness\nExample: Auth-based routing where authorization headers are modified\n\n**Scenario C: Never Clear (Conservative)**\n```yaml\n# Route cache never clears, maximizing performance\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\nUse when: External processor never modifies routing-affecting headers, or you want to prioritize cache efficiency\nExample: Logging/monitoring-only external processor\n\n---\n\n### 2. Observability Mode with Deferred Stream Closure\n\n**What's new:**\n- `observability_mode: true` enables \"send and go\" behavior\n- External processor streams can be kept open longer than the main request/response flow\n- New `deferred_close_timeout` field controls how long streams are held open before closure\n\n**How it works:**\n\nIn observability mode:\n1. Envoy sends request and response data to the external processor without waiting for responses\n2. The external processor acts as a passive observer/logger\n3. The gRPC stream remains open after the request/response completes (deferred closure)\n4. Stream closes after `deferred_close_timeout` expires (default: 5 seconds)\n\n**Configuration:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Optional, default is 5000ms\n\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Processing mode restrictions in observability mode:**\n- \u2705 Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is fully supported\n- \u2705 `NONE` mode (skip body) works as expected\n- \u26a0\ufe0f Other modes (`BUFFERED`, `BUFFERED_PARTIAL`) are ignored; behavior falls back to streaming\n\n**Key behavioral differences:**\n- External processor should **not** send responses (they are ignored)\n- `message_timeout` restrictions don't apply (stream remains open indefinitely until deferred timeout)\n- Flow control is still being developed; use with caution on high-throughput systems (see GitHub issue #33319)\n\n**New configuration fields:**\n\n| Field | Type | Default | Description |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `observability_mode` | bool | false | Enable send-and-go observation mode |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | Duration | 5000ms | How long to keep stream open after request/response completes |\n\n**Example use cases:**\n- Passive telemetry collection\n- Non-invasive traffic monitoring\n- Distributed tracing integration\n- Observability data extraction without modifying traffic\n\n---\n\n### 3. Thread-Local Stream Management\n\n**What's new:**\n- Internal stream management improvements for observability mode\n- `ThreadLocalStreamManager` handles deferred stream cleanup\n- Improved resource management for long-lived streams\n\n**Impact on configuration:**\n- This is an internal implementation detail\n- No configuration changes needed\n- Automatically used when `observability_mode` is enabled\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Audit Current Route Cache Configuration\n\n1. Review all ext_proc filter configurations in your environment:\n   ```bash\n   # Search for ext_proc filters in your configs\n   grep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" *.yaml\n   ```\n\n2. Note which configurations use `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### Step 2: Plan Route Cache Strategy\n\nFor each configuration with `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:\n\n| Current Behavior | New Configuration | Rationale |\n|---|---|---|\n| External processor never modifies routing headers | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Preserve performance optimization |\n| External processor sometimes modifies routing headers | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Let processor control cache |\n| External processor always affects routing | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Ensure correct routing decisions |\n\n### Step 3: Update Configuration Files\n\n**Example migration:**\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n### Step 4: Optional - Enable Observability Mode (for new deployments)\n\nIf you need non-invasive monitoring:\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      observability_mode: true\n      deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: STREAMED\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### Step 5: Validate Configuration\n\n1. Validate YAML syntax:\n   ```bash\n   envoy -c config.yaml --mode validate_config\n   ```\n\n2. Check for configuration conflicts:\n   - Ensure only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` is set\n   - If observability mode is enabled, verify processing mode is compatible\n\n3. Test in staging environment with representative traffic\n\n### Step 6: Deploy and Monitor\n\n1. Deploy updated configuration to one canary instance\n2. Monitor for:\n   - Route cache hit/miss ratios\n   - Ext_proc filter statistics (clear_route_cache_* counters)\n   - gRPC stream health\n3. Gradually roll out to remaining instances\n4. Compare performance metrics before/after\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Configuration Validation Tests\n\n**Test mutual exclusivity:**\n```bash\n# This should fail validation\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Test enum values:**\n```bash\n# Test each value separately\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 2. Route Cache Behavior Tests\n\n**Scenario: DEFAULT behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\nExpected: Route cache clears when external processor response has `clear_route_cache: true`\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache should clear\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache should remain\n- \u2705 Returns with no cache directive \u2192 cache should remain\n\n**Scenario: CLEAR behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\nExpected: Route cache always clears regardless of processor response\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache clears (expected)\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache still clears (verify this works)\n\n**Scenario: RETAIN behavior**\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\nExpected: Route cache never clears\n\nTest with processor that:\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 cache should NOT clear\n- \u2705 Returns `clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 cache should NOT clear\n\n### 3. Observability Mode Tests\n\n**Test configuration validation:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 3s\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: STREAMED  # \u2705 OK\n  response_body_mode: BUFFERED # \u26a0\ufe0f Will be ignored\n```\n\n**Test stream lifecycle:**\n1. Start Envoy with observability_mode enabled\n2. Send request through proxy\n3. Monitor gRPC stream:\n   - Stream should remain open after response completes\n   - Stream should close after `deferred_close_timeout` expires\n4. Verify external processor receives all data without responding\n\n**Test flow control (with caution):**\n- Send high-volume traffic through observability mode\n- Monitor for buffer overflow or dropped messages\n- Check warning at GitHub issue #33319\n\n### 4. Backward Compatibility Tests\n\n**Test old configuration still works:**\n```yaml\n# v1.30 style should still work\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\nExpected: Configuration loads without error and behaves like `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n### 5. Performance Tests\n\n**Before/after comparison:**\n\n| Metric | Target | How to measure |\n|---|---|---|\n| Route cache hit ratio | \u2265 95% (RETAIN) | Envoy admin /stats with cache stats |\n| Ext_proc latency | < 200ms p99 | external_processor.message_timeout_ms metric |\n| gRPC stream count | Stable | Prometheus or Envoy /stats |\n| Memory usage | \u00b1 5% | Container memory usage |\n\n**Test scenarios:**\n1. Conservative (RETAIN) vs. default behavior \u2192 expect better cache hit ratio\n2. Aggressive (CLEAR) vs. default \u2192 expect more route recomputations\n3. Observability mode without request/response body \u2192 expect lower latency than normal mode\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Quick Rollback (Less than 1 minute downtime)\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrade:\n\n1. **Immediately revert configuration:**\n   ```yaml\n   # Instead of new style:\n   # route_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n   # Use old compatible style:\n   disable_clear_route_cache: false\n   ```\n\n2. **Reload Envoy without restart:**\n   ```bash\n   kill -HUP <envoy_pid>  # Graceful reload\n   ```\n\n3. **Verify service health:**\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep ext_proc\n   ```\n\n### Extended Rollback (Staged revert)\n\nIf using infrastructure as code:\n\n1. Revert configuration files to v1.30 versions\n2. Perform canary deployment on one instance\n3. Monitor for stability (5-10 minutes)\n4. Complete rollback to remaining instances\n\n### Full Version Rollback (if needed)\n\nIf issues are critical:\n\n1. Preserve data/state from v1.31 deployment\n2. Download v1.30.0 binary (if still available)\n3. Deploy v1.30.0 with previous configuration\n4. Investigate root cause before re-upgrading\n\n**Recovery steps post-rollback:**\n- Check Envoy logs for configuration errors\n- Verify external processor service compatibility\n- Review any custom filter extensions for compatibility\n- Test thoroughly in staging before retry\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Using Both Fields Simultaneously\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflict!\n```\n\n**Solution:**\nChoose one approach. The configuration validator will catch this:\n```yaml\n# Choose EITHER the old style:\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# OR the new style:\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Wrong RouteCacheAction for Use Case\n\n**Problem:**\nUsing `CLEAR` when external processor only logs traffic, causing unnecessary route recomputation overhead.\n\n**Solution:**\nProfile your external processor behavior:\n```bash\n# In your processor, log which responses set clear_route_cache\nlog.info(\"Request headers changed: {}\", header_modified)\n```\n\nThen use appropriate action:\n```yaml\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN  # If processor doesn't modify routing headers\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT # If processor selectively modifies headers\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR   # If processor often modifies routing headers\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Observability Mode Without Proper Timeouts\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\n# deferred_close_timeout not set (uses default 5s)\n```\nMay cause unexpected stream behavior if not aligned with request timeouts.\n\n**Solution:**\nExplicitly set timeout matching your infrastructure:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\ndeferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Explicit for observability\n```\n\nEnsure it's longer than typical response time but shorter than upstream timeouts.\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode with Incompatible Body Modes\n\n**Problem:**\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: BUFFERED  # Not officially supported in observability mode\n```\n\n**Solution:**\nUse only STREAMED mode:\n```yaml\nobservability_mode: true\nprocessing_mode:\n  request_body_mode: STREAMED   # \u2705 Correct\n  response_body_mode: STREAMED  # \u2705 Correct\n```\n\n---\n\n## Statistics Changes\n\n### New Statistics in v1.31\n\nThe ext_proc filter continues to use the same statistics namespace but handles route cache events differently based on the new `route_cache_action` enum.\n\n**Existing statistics still available:**\n- `clear_route_cache_ignored` - Requests to clear cache that were ignored\n- `clear_route_cache_disabled` - Cache clears that were explicitly disabled\n\n**Behavioral change:**\nWhen using `route_cache_action`:\n- If set to `RETAIN`, all external processor requests to clear cache are counted in `clear_route_cache_disabled`\n- If set to `CLEAR`, cache is always cleared (fewer `clear_route_cache_ignored` events)\n- If set to `DEFAULT`, behavior matches v1.30\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Reference\n\n### Complete v1.31 ext_proc Configuration Example\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n\n      # Required: gRPC service configuration\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n        timeout: 2s\n\n      # Optional: how to handle processor unavailability\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n\n      # Optional: route cache control (choose ONE)\n      # New style (recommended):\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN  # DEFAULT, CLEAR, or RETAIN\n\n      # Old style (still supported, but deprecated):\n      # disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n      # Optional: processing mode configuration\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        response_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        request_trailer_mode: SEND\n        response_trailer_mode: SKIP\n\n      # Optional: attributes to send to processor\n      request_attributes:\n        - request.path\n        - request.method\n      response_attributes:\n        - response.code\n\n      # Optional: mutation rules for headers\n      mutation_rules:\n        allow_all_routing: false\n        allow_envoy: true\n        allow_other_origins: false\n\n      # Optional: header forwarding rules\n      forward_rules:\n        allowed_headers:\n          patterns:\n            - prefix: \"x-custom\"\n\n      # Optional: observability mode\n      observability_mode: false\n      deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n\n      # Optional: metadata handling\n      metadata_options:\n        forwarding_namespaces:\n          untyped:\n            - \"my.custom.namespace\"\n        receiving_namespaces:\n          untyped:\n            - \"ext_proc_result\"\n\n      # Optional: statistics prefix (to distinguish multiple ext_proc filters)\n      stat_prefix: \"my_ext_proc_\"\n\n      # Optional: additional filter state metadata\n      filter_metadata:\n        version: \"1.31\"\n        environment: \"production\"\n\n      # Optional: allow external processor to override processing mode\n      allow_mode_override: true\n\n      # Optional: ignore immediate_response from processor\n      disable_immediate_response: false\n\n      # Optional: max override timeout allowed from processor\n      max_message_timeout: 30s\n\n      # Message timeout for each gRPC message\n      message_timeout: 200ms\n```\n\n---\n\n## Version Compatibility Matrix\n\n| Component | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Proto API version | v3 | v3 | Same major version |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2705 Full support | \u2705 Supported (legacy) | Transitional in v1.31 |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 Full support | New in v1.31 |\n| `observability_mode` | \u2705 Present | \u2705 Enhanced | Stream lifecycle improved |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 New | Controls observability mode timing |\n| External processor protocol | gRPC v1 | gRPC v1 | No protocol changes |\n| Backward config compat | N/A | \u2705 High | Old configs work mostly as-is |\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n### Proto Definitions\n- **Configuration:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- **Processing Mode:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto`\n\n### Implementation Files\n- **Filter Header:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n- **Filter Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n- **Configuration:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/config.cc`\n\n### Documentation\n- **Filter Documentation:** `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`\n- **API Reference:** Envoy v3 API reference for ExternalProcessor message\n\n### Related Issues\n- **GitHub #33319:** Flow control in observability mode (still in development)\n- **Proto Migration Annotations:** `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto`\n\n---\n\n## FAQ\n\n**Q: Can I use both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` in the same config?**\nA: No. The configuration validator will reject configurations that set both fields. Choose one approach based on your version and compatibility needs.\n\n**Q: Is observability mode production-ready in v1.31.0?**\nA: Yes, but with a caveat. The feature is production-ready for basic use (reading logs/metrics). However, flow control mechanisms are still being developed (GitHub issue #33319), so use caution with extremely high-throughput systems.\n\n**Q: What happens if I set an invalid `route_cache_action` value?**\nA: Configuration validation will fail during startup with a clear error message. Valid values are `DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, or `RETAIN`.\n\n**Q: Do I need to change my external processor code?**\nA: No. The external processor protocol (gRPC messages) hasn't changed between v1.30 and v1.31. Your processor code should work without modification.\n\n**Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?**\nA: Ask: \"Does my external processor ever modify headers that affect routing decisions?\" If yes and selectively, use `DEFAULT`. If always, use `CLEAR`. If never, use `RETAIN`.\n\n**Q: Can I change `route_cache_action` at runtime?**\nA: Not directly via admin API in v1.31. You must update the configuration and perform a graceful reload (`SIGHUP` on process ID or configuration push through control plane).\n\n**Q: What's the performance impact of changing from `RETAIN` to `CLEAR`?**\nA: Minimal direct impact from the enum choice itself. The performance difference comes from increased route recomputation frequency. Measure route cache hit ratio before/after.\n\n---\n\n## Summary Checklist\n\nUse this checklist for your migration:\n\n- [ ] **Audit:** Found and documented all `disable_clear_route_cache` usage\n- [ ] **Plan:** Decided on appropriate `route_cache_action` for each config\n- [ ] **Update:** Migrated configurations to v1.31 style or verified backward compatibility\n- [ ] **Validate:** Ran configuration validator and resolved any conflicts\n- [ ] **Test:** Tested in staging with representative traffic\n- [ ] **Monitor:** Set up dashboards for route cache and ext_proc statistics\n- [ ] **Deploy:** Canary deployment to one instance\n- [ ] **Observe:** Monitored metrics for 10-15 minutes\n- [ ] **Rollout:** Gradual rollout to remaining instances\n- [ ] **Document:** Updated internal documentation with new configuration approach\n- [ ] **Archive:** Backed up v1.30 configurations for rollback if needed\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated:** 2024\n**Envoy Versions:** v1.30.0 \u2192 v1.31.0\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide
## Upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0

## Overview

This migration guide covers the upgrade of the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The 1.31.0 release introduces enhanced route cache management with a new enum-based approach, support for observability mode with deferred stream closure, and improved stream lifecycle management.

Key highlights of this release:
- **New `route_cache_action` enum** replaces boolean flag-based route cache control
- **Observability mode enhancements** with deferred stream closure and configurable timeouts
- **Improved stream management** via thread-local stream managers for better resource cleanup

Most configurations will continue to work with minimal or no changes, though some optimizations are recommended for new deployments.

---

## Breaking Changes

### 1. Route Cache Control Field Reorganization

**What changed:**
- The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11 in v1.30) is being **transitioned to a new enum-based system** using `route_cache_action` (field 18 in v1.31)
- A new `RouteCacheAction` enum provides three explicit states instead of just binary on/off

**Migration impact:** ⚠️ **Low to Moderate**
- Existing configurations using `disable_clear_route_cache` will **continue to work** due to backward compatibility
- However, Envoy's internal code now treats these as different representations that may not remain synchronized in future versions
- New configurations should use the enum approach

**Before (v1.30):**
```yaml
ext_proc:
  grpc_service:
    envoy_grpc:
      cluster_name: ext_proc_service
  disable_clear_route_cache: true
```

**After (v1.31 - Recommended):**
```yaml
ext_proc:
  grpc_
... (truncated)
